If you have extremely thin/delicate hair, you may be able to completely dry your hair with it but for longer, thicker hair, I think it would take you a long time and you'd likely wear out the dryer fairly quickly.<br /><br />I've been very satisfied with the life-span of this inexpensive but oh-so-handy tool. I've never had one actually die on me. Rather, as the air brush ages (and after LOTS of use)the motor(which is very small) may overheat causing the dryer to stop working until it cools down. I've not had it stop running while using it. Instead, if I turn it off momentarily, I can hear a click (the internal, automatic shut-off) and the dryer won't run again until it has safely cooled off. This can be annoying and time consuming so to me, that's when it's time to get a new one. Also, if you use hair products, after a long period of repeated use, the brush will get an icky build up on it, as would any tool. There's a screw-off cap at the end of the barrel which allows you to remove the brush to clean it. I found that warm water, a soft nail brush and liquid soap provide great results.<br /><br />Overall, I think this is an excellent tool at a very low price, one which I've not been able to find anywhere except Amazon. I recommend it to anyone with short to medium length and fine to medium thickness hair.
